# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Investigation: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

**Repository:** prometheus/prometheus
**Task Type:** Cross-Service Debug (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After a Prometheus upgrade, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The issue correlates with target discovery changes — when targets are added or removed, some remote-write shards stall.

Prometheus logs show:
```
level=info msg="Resharding queues" from=4 to=6
level=info msg="Resharding done" numShards=6
```

But after resharding, metrics show some shards have `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` stuck at >0 with no progress.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. How remote-write queue resharding works (which files/functions)
2. What changed in the resharding logic recently
3. The specific mechanism causing shards to stall
4. Why the issue is intermittent (timing/race condition)
5. Which metrics or logs would confirm the root cause

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `storage/remote/` package, particularly queue management and shard calculation


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

57-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the remote-write queue resharding failure in Prometheus. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Root Cause:** A race condition in the resharding logic introduced when timestamp tracking was moved from WriteStorage-level to QueueManager-level. When resharding occurs, the per-queue `highestTimestamp` metric becomes stale, causing incorrect shard calculations that can lead to deadlocks when queues are full.

**Specific Mechanism:**
1. Resharding moves `highestTimestamp` tracking to per-QueueManager level
2. During resharding transitions, old shards shut down while new ones start up
3. The new QueueManager doesn't reflect samples still in old shards
4. Stale timestamp → incorrect delay calculation → wrong desired shard count
5. When queue is full, this prevents proper scaling, causing stalls

**Why It's Intermittent:**
- Only occurs under specific conditions: high load + slow backend + frequent resharding
- Depends on timing of samples arriving during shard transitions
- Can be masked if samples arrive slowly enough to update metrics before next calculation

**The Fix:** Commit 6806b68 correctly reverted the problematic changes and restored:
- WriteStorage-level timestamp and sample rate tracking
- Separate tracking of dropped (by relabeling) samples
- Proper formula that accounts for data retention ratio

The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with detailed evidence, code references, and diagnostic recommendations.

enableExemplarRemoteWrite, enableNativeHistogramRemoteWrite, walMetadata)\n541: \n542: \t// The current MetadataWatcher implementation is mutually exclusive\n543: \t// with the new approach, which context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n562: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n563: \tif t.protoMsg != remoteapi.WriteV1MessageType {\n564: \t\treturn\n565: \t}\n566: \n567: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n568: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n569: \tfor _, entry sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n591: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n592: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n593: \tif err != nil {\n594: \t\treturn err\n595: \t}\n596: \n597: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n598: \n599: \tattemptStore := \t\t\tspan.SetAttributes(semconv.HTTPResendCount(try))\n612: \t\t}\n613: \n614: \t\tbegin := time.Now()\n615: \t\t// Ignoring WriteResponseStats, because there is nothing for metadata, since \n620: \t\tif err != nil {\n621: \t\t\tspan.RecordError(err)\n622: \t\t\treturn err\n623: \t\t}\n624: \t\treturn nil\n625: \t}\n626: \n627: \tretry := func() {\n628: sampleAgeLimit time.Duration, ts int64) bool {\n640: \tif sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n641: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n642: \t\treturn false\n643: \t}\n644: \tlimitTs := baseTime.Add(-sampleAgeLimit)\n645: \tsampleTs := timestamp.Time(ts)\n646: \treturn sampleTs.Before(limitTs)\n647: }\n648: \n649: // timeSeriesAgeChecker encapsulates the logic for checking if time series data is too old.\n650: type timeSeriesAgeChecker struct {\n651: \tmetrics        *queueManagerMetrics\n652: \tbaseTime       time.Time\n653: \tsampleAgeLimit time.Duration\n654: }\n655: \n656: // checkAndRecordIfOld checks if a timestamp is too old and records the appropriate metric.\n657: // Returns true if the data should be dropped.\n658: func (c *timeSeriesAgeChecker) checkAndRecordIfOld(timestamp int64, dataType string) bool {\n659: \tif c.sampleAgeLimit == 0 {\n660: \t\t// If sampleAgeLimit is unset, then we never skip samples due to their age.\n661: \t\treturn false\n662: \t}\n663: \n664: \tif !isSampleOld(c.baseTime, c.sampleAgeLimit, timestamp) {\n665: \t\treturn false\n666: \t}\n667: \n668: \t// Record the drop in metrics.\n669: \tswitch dataType {\n670: \tcase \"sample\":\n671: \t\tc.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n672: \tcase \"histogram\":\n673: \t\tc.metrics.droppedHistogramsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n674: \tcase \"exemplar\":\n675: \t\tc.metrics.droppedExemplarsTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n676: \t}\n677: \treturn true\n678: }\n679: \n680: func isTimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n681: \tchecker := &timeSeriesAgeChecker{\n682: \t\tmetrics:        metrics,\n683: \t\tbaseTime:       baseTime,\n684: \t\tsampleAgeLimit: sampleAgeLimit,\n685: \t}\n686: \n687: \treturn func(ts prompb.TimeSeries) bool {\n688: \t\t// Only the first element should be set in the series, therefore we only check the first element.\n689: \t\tswitch {\n690: \t\tcase len(ts.Samples) > 0:\n691: \t\t\treturn \t\tcase len(ts.Exemplars) > 0:\n695: \t\t\treturn checker.checkAndRecordIfOld(ts.Exemplars[0].Timestamp, \"exemplar\")\n696: \t\tdefault:\n697: \t\t\treturn false\n698: \t\t}\n699: \t}\n700: }\n701: \n702: func isV2TimeSeriesOldFilter(metrics *queueManagerMetrics, baseTime time.Time, sampleAgeLimit time.Duration) func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n703: \tchecker := &timeSeriesAgeChecker{\n704: \t\tmetrics:        metrics,\n705: \t\tbaseTime:       baseTime,\n706: \t\tsampleAgeLimit: sampleAgeLimit,\n707: \t}\n708: \n709: \treturn func(ts writev2.TimeSeries) bool {\n710: \t\t// Only the \n724: // Append queues a sample to be sent to the remote storage. Blocks until all samples are\n725: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n726: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n727: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n728: outer:\n729: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n730: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n731: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n732: \t\t\tcontinue\n733: \t\t}\n734: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n735: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n736: \t\tif !ok {\n737: \t\t\tt.dataDropped.incr(1)\n738: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n739: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n740: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n741: \t\t\t} else {\n742: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n743: \t\t\t}\n744: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n745: \t\t\tcontinue\n746: \t\t}\n747: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n748: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n749: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n750: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n751: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n752: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n753: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n754: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n755: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n756: \t\tfor {\n757: \t\t\tselect {\n758: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n759: \t\t\t\treturn false\n760: \t\t\tdefault:\n761: \t\t\t}\n762: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n763: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n764: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n765: \t\t\t\ttimestamp:    s.T,\n766: \t\t\t\tvalue:        s.V,\n767: \t\t\t\tsType:        tSample,\n768: \t\t\t}) {\n769: \t\t\t\tcontinue outer\n770: \t\t\t}\n771: \n772: \t\t\tt.metrics.enqueueRetriesTotal.Inc()\n773: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n774: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n775: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n776: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n777: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n778: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n779: \t\t\t}\n780: \t\t}\n781: \t}\n782: \treturn true\n783: }\n784: \n785: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n786: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n787: \t\treturn true\n788: \t}\n789: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n790: outer:\n791: \tfor _, e := \treturn true\n901: }\n902: \n903: func (t *QueueManager) AppendFloatHistograms(floatHistograms []record.RefFloatHistogramSample) bool {\n904: \tif !t.sendNativeHistograms {\n905: \t\treturn \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n971: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n972: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n973: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Start()\n979: \t}\n980: \n981: \tt.wg.Add(2)\n982: \tgo t.updateShardsLoop()\n983: \tgo t.reshardLoop()\n984: }\n985: \n986: // Stop stops sending samples to the remote storage and waits for pending\n987: // sends to complete.\n988: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n989: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n990: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n991: \n992: \tclose(t.quit)\n993: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n994: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n995: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n996: \tt.wg.Wait()\n997: \tt.shards.stop()\n998: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n999: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n1000: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n1001: \t}\n1002: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n1003: }\n1004: \n1005: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n1006: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n1007: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n1008: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n1009: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n1010: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n1011: \tfor _, s := range series {\n1012: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert Used when only client specific\n1075: // fields are updated to avoid restarting the queue.\n1076: func (t *QueueManager) SetClient(c WriteClient) {\n1077: \tt.clientMtx.Lock()\n1078: \tt.storeClient = c\n1079: \tt.clientMtx.Unlock()\n1080: }\n1081: \n1082: func (t *QueueManager) client() WriteClient {\n1083: \tt.clientMtx.RLock()\n1084: \tdefer t.clientMtx.RUnlock()\n1085: \treturn t.storeClient\n1086: }\n1087: \n1088: // processExternalLabels merges externalLabels into b. t.wg.Done()\n1100: \n1101: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1102: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1103: \tfor {\n1104: \t\tselect {\n1105: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1106: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1107: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1108: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1109: \t\t\t}\n1110: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1111: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1112: \t\t\tselect {\n1113: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1114: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1115: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1116: \t\t\tdefault:\n1117: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1118: \t\t\t}\n1119: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1120: \t\t\treturn\n1121: \t\t}\n1122: \t}\n1123: }\n1124: \n1125: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1126: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1127: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1128: \t\treturn false\n1129: \t}\n1130: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1131: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1132: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1133: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1134: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1135: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1136: \t\treturn false\n1137: \t}\n1138: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1139: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1140: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1141: \n1142: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1143: \t\treturn false\n1144: \t}\n1145: \treturn true\n1146: }\n1147: \n1148: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1149: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1150: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1151: // based on the return value.\n1152: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1153: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1154: \tt.dataDropped.tick()\n1155: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1156: \n1157: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1158: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1159: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1160: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1161: \tvar (\n1162: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1163: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1164: \t\tdataKeptRatio   = dataOutRate / (t.dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)\n1165: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1166: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate*dataKeptRatio - dataOutRate\n1167: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1168: \t\thighestRecv     = t.highestRecvTimestamp.Get()\n1169: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1170: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate * dataKeptRatio\n1171: \t)\n1172: \n1173: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1174: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1175: \t}\n1176: \n1177: \tvar (\n1178: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1179: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1180: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1181: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1182: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate*dataKeptRatio + backlogCatchup)\n1183: \t)\n1184: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1185: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1186: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1187: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1188: \t\t\"dataKeptRatio\", dataKeptRatio,\n1189: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1190: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1191: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1192: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1193: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1194: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1195: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1196: \t)\n1197: \n1198: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1199: \tvar (\n1200: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1201: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1202: \t)\n1203: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1204: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1205: \n1206: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1207: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1208: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1209: \t}\n1210: \n1211: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1212: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1213: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1214: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1215: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1216: \t}\n1217: \n1218: \tswitch {\n1219: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1220: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1221: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1222: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1223: \t}\n1224: \treturn numShards\n1225: }\n1226: \n1227: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1228: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1229: \n1230: \tfor {\n1231: \t\tselect {\n1232: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1233: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1234: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1235: \t\t\t// order.\n1236: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1237: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1238: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1239: \t\t\treturn\n1240: \t\t}\n1241: \t}\n1242: }\n1243: \n1244: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1245: \ts := &shards{\n1246: \t\tqm:   t,\n1247: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1248: \t}\n1249: \treturn s\n1250: }\n1251: \n1252: type shards struct {\n1253: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1254: \n1255: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1256: \tqueues []*queue\n1257: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1258: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1259: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1260: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1261: \n1262: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1263: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1264: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1265: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1266: \n1267: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1268: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1269: \n1270: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1271: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1272: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1273: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown    atomic.Uint32\n1274: \texemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown  atomic.Uint32\n1275: \thistogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown atomic.Uint32\n1276: \tmetadataDroppedOnHardShutdown   atomic.Uint32\n1277: }\n1278: \n1279: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1280: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \n1284: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1285: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1286: \n1287: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1288: \tfor i := range n {\n1289: \t\tnewQueues[i] = newQueue(s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend, s.qm.cfg.Capacity)\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \ts.queues = newQueues\n1293: \n1294: \tvar hardShutdownCtx context.Context\n1295: \thardShutdownCtx, s.hardShutdown = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1296: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1297: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1298: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1299: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1300: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1301: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1302: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1303: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1304: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1305: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1306: \tfor i := range n {\n1307: \t\tgo s.runShard(hardShutdownCtx, i, newQueues[i])\n1308: \t}\n1309: }\n1310: \n1311: // stop the shards; subsequent call to enqueue will return false.\n1312: func (s *shards) stop() {\n1313: \t// Attempt a clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1314: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1315: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1316: \t// RLock here.\n1317: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1318: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1319: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1320: \n1321: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1322: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1323: \t// send on closed channel.\n1324: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1325: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1326: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1327: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1328: \t}\n1329: \tselect {\n1330: \tcase <-s.done:\n1331: \t\treturn\n1332: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1333: \t}\n1334: \n1335: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1336: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1337: \t<-s.done\n1338: \n1339: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1340: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1341: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1342: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1343: \t\t}\n1344: \t}\n1345: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1346: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1347: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1348: }\n1349: \n1350: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1351: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1352: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1353: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1354: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1355: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1356: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1357: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1358: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1359: \tselect {\n1360: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1361: \t\treturn false\n1362: \tdefault:\n1363: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1364: \t\tif !appended {\n1365: \t\t\treturn false\n1366: \t\t}\n1367: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1368: \t\tcase tSample:\n1369: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1370: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1371: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1372: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingExemplars.Inc()\n1373: \t\t\ts.enqueuedExemplars.Inc()\n1374: \t\tcase tHistogram, tFloatHistogram:\n1375: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Inc()\n1376: \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1377: \t\tdefault:\n1378: \t\t\treturn true\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1381: \t\treturn true\n1382: \t}\n1383: }\n1384: \n1385: type queue struct {\n1386: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1387: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1388: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1389: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1390: \n1391: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1392: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1393: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1394: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1395: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1396: }\n1397: \n1398: type timeSeries struct {\n1399: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1400: \tvalue          float64\n1401: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1402: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1403: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1404: \ttimestamp      int64\n1405: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1406: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1407: \tsType seriesType\n1408: }\n1409: \n1410: type seriesType int\n1411: \n1412: const (\n1413: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1414: \ttExemplar\n1415: \ttHistogram\n1416: \ttFloatHistogram\n1417: \ttMetadata\n1418: )\n1419: \n1420: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1421: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1422: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1423: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1424: \tif batches == 0 {\n1425: \t\tbatches = 1\n1426: \t}\n1427: \treturn &queue{\n1428: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1429: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1430: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1431: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1432: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1437: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1438: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1439: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1440: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1441: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1442: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1443: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1444: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1445: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1446: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1447: \t\tselect {\n1448: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1449: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1450: \t\t\treturn true\n1451: \t\tdefault:\n1452: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1453: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1454: \t\t\treturn false\n1455: \t\t}\n1456: \t}\n1457: \treturn true\n1458: }\n1459: \n1460: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1461: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1462: }\n1463: \n1464: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1465: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1466: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1467: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1468: \tselect {\n1469: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1470: \t\treturn batch\n1471: \tdefault:\n1472: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1473: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1474: \t\treturn batch\n1475: \t}\n1476: }\n1477: \n1478: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1479: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1483: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1484: \t}\n1485: }\n1486: \n1487: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1488: // made after this is called.\n1489: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1490: loop:\n1491: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1492: \t\tselect {\n1493: \t\tcase <-done:\n1494: \t\t\tbreak loop\n1495: \t\tcase <-time.After(time.Second):\n1496: \t\t}\n1497: \t}\n1498: \n1499: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1500: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1501: \tq.batch = nil\n1502: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1503: }\n1504: \n1505: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1506: // be retried it will return true.\n1507: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1508: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1509: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1510: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1511: \t\treturn false\n1512: \t}\n1513: \n1514: \tselect {\n1515: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1516: \t\treturn false\n1517: \tcase <-done:\n1518: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1519: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1520: \t\treturn false\n1521: \tdefault:\n1522: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1523: \t\treturn true\n1524: \t}\n1525: }\n1526: \n1527: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1528: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1529: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1530: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1531: \tif batches > 0 {\n1532: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1533: \t\tq.batchPool = *queue) {\n1540: \tdefer func() {\n1541: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1542: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1543: \t\t}\n1544: \t}()\n1545: \n1546: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1547: \tsymbolTable := failed.\n1614: \t\t\tdroppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n1615: \t\t\tdroppedExemplars := int(s.enqueuedExemplars.Load())\n1616: \t\t\tdroppedHistograms := \n1652: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1653: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms int\n1654: \tfor nPending, d := range batch {\n1655: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = pendingData[nPending].Samples[:0]\n1656: \t\tif sendExemplars {\n1657: pendingData[nPending].Histograms[:0]\n1661: \t\t}\n1662: \n1663: \t\t// Number of pending samples is limited by the fact that sendSamples (via sendSamplesWithBackoff)\n1664: \t\t// retries endlessly, so once we reach max samples, if we can never send to the endpoint we'll\n1665: \t\t// stop reading from the queue. This makes it safe to reference pendingSamples by index.\n1666: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Labels = prompb.FromLabels(d.seriesLabels, pendingData[nPending].Labels)\n1667: \n1668: \t\tswitch d.sType {\n1669: \t\tcase tSample:\n1670: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = append(pendingData[nPending].Samples, prompb.Sample{\n1671: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1672: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1673: \t\t\t})\n1674: \t\t\tnPendingSamples++\n1675: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1676: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Exemplars = append(pendingData[nPending].Exemplars, prompb.Exemplar{\n1677: \t\t\t\tLabels:    prompb.FromLabels(d.exemplarLabels, nil),\n1678: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1679: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1680: \t\t\t})\n1681: \t\t\tnPendingExemplars++\n1682: \t\tcase tHistogram:\n1683: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromIntHistogram(d.timestamp, d.histogram))\n1684: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1685: \t\tcase tFloatHistogram:\n1686: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromFloatHistogram(d.timestamp, d.floatHistogram))\n1687: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1688: \t\t}\n1689: \t}\n1690: \treturn nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms\n1691: }\n1692: \n1693: func (s *shards) sendSamples(ctx context.Context, WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1710: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1711: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1712: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1713:   "content": "# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nThe resharding stall occurs due to a race condition in the sharding metric calculations introduced in commit 184c7eb (\"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\"). When shards are computed at the QueueManager level rather than the WriteStorage level, the `highestTimestamp` metric becomes stale during resharding transitions, causing the `calculateDesiredShards()` function to incorrectly calculate shard requirements and potentially stall when queues are full.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1152-1224` (calculateDesiredShards function)\n\nThe root cause is a data collection and timing mismatch introduced when resharding logic moved timestamp tracking from WriteStorage-level to QueueManager-level:\n\n1. **Metric Location Change:** In commit 184c7eb, `highestTimestamp` moved from `metrics.highestTimestamp` (WriteStorage-wide) to `qm.highestRecvTimestamp` (per QueueManager). This per-queue metric is updated only when samples are **enqueued into the shard** (line 1380 in queue_manager.go).\n\n2. **Race Condition During Resharding:** When resharding occurs (shards.stop() \u2192 shards.start()), the following happens:\n   - Old shards are shut down, draining their queues\n   - New shards are created and started\n   - During this transition, **samples arriving at WriteStorage are temporarily routed to the old shard instances**\n   - The new QueueManager's `highestRecvTimestamp` doesn't reflect samples from the old shards because they were already enqueued to the old instance\n   - This creates a timestamp gap\n\n3. **Incorrect Shard Calculation:** In `calculateDesiredShards()` at lines 1167-1171:\n   ```go\n   highestRecv     = t.highestRecvTimestamp.Get()  // Per-queue metric, may be stale\n   highestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n   delay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n   dataPending     = delay * dataInRate * dataKeptRatio\n   ```\n\n   If `highestRecv` is significantly behind `highestSent` (or zero after resharding), the `dataPending` calculation becomes invalid, leading to incorrect `desiredShards` calculation.\n\n4. **Deadlock/Stall Scenario:** When the queue is full and resharding is triggered:\n   - `shards.stop()` attempts to flush all data (line 1236)\n   - New incoming samples must be dropped or blocked\n   - But the resharding calculation is stale, preventing proper shard scaling\n   - This can cause a deadlock if `Append()` blocks while resharding is in progress\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**File:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`\n\n1. **Line 1280-1308:** `shards.start()` creates new queues but doesn't inherit timestamp state from old shards:\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // Metrics reset\n       s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n\n       newQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n       for i := range n {\n           newQueues[i] = newQueue(...)\n       }\n       s.queues = newQueues  // Old queues discarded\n   ```\n\n2. **Line 1355-1382:** `enqueue()` is the only place where per-queue `highestTimestamp` is updated:\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) enqueue(...) bool {\n       ...\n       s.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))  // Updated here only\n       return true\n   }\n   ```\n\n3. **Line 1152-1171:** `calculateDesiredShards()` uses the per-queue timestamp which becomes stale:\n   ```go\n   highestRecv     = t.highestRecvTimestamp.Get()  // Stale after resharding\n   highestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n   delay           = highestRecv - highestSent     // Can be wrong or negative\n   ```\n\n4. **Line 1227-1241:** `reshardLoop()` stops old shards before starting new ones:\n   ```go\n   case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n       t.shards.stop()      // Old shards shut down\n       t.shards.start(numShards)  // New shards initialized\n   ```\n\n### Commit History\n\n- **184c7eb (2025-08-20):** \"storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level\" - Introduced the per-queue metric\n- **6806b68 (2025-10-29):** \"[release-3.7] fix: Remote-write: revert changes in the queue resharding logic\" - Reverted the problematic commit\n- **35c3232 (2025-11-14):** Marked the test `TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock` as flaky due to deadlocks\n- **e799952 (2025-11-25):** Re-enabled the test with improved reliability\n\n### Test Evidence\n\nThe test at `cmd/prometheus/main_test.go:977-1050` (`TestRemoteWrite_ReshardingWithoutDeadlock`) was created specifically to catch this issue. It:\n- Creates a slow remote storage backend (1-second latency)\n- Limits queue capacity to force full queues\n- Monitors `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` to verify resharding succeeds\n- Previously failed due to deadlock when queues were full during resharding\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go**\n   - `QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards()` - Uses stale timestamp metrics\n   - `shards.start()` - Doesn't preserve timestamp state across resharding\n   - `shards.enqueue()` - Only updates per-queue timestamp, not reflected in old shards\n\n2. **storage/remote/write.go**\n   - `timestampTracker.Commit()` - Increments global `samplesIn` but not per-queue metric during resharding\n\n3. **Metrics Affected**\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds` - Per-queue, becomes stale\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` - Calculated from stale timestamp\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - Can become stuck if resharding stalls\n\n## Why the Issue is Intermittent\n\n1. **Timing-dependent:** The race only manifests when:\n   - Resharding is triggered (high throughput detected)\n   - Queue is near capacity\n   - Target discovery changes cause resharding (from the issue description)\n\n2. **Load-dependent:** The issue is more likely under:\n   - High sample arrival rate (pushes shards to capacity)\n   - Slow remote backend (high latency, low throughput)\n   - Frequent target discovery changes (frequent resharding attempts)\n\n3. **Not always detectable:** If samples trickle in slowly, the old shard metrics may update before the next calculation cycle, masking the issue.\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe revert in commit 6806b68 was the correct fix. The proper solution is:\n\n1. **Restore WriteStorage-level timestamp tracking** - Move `highestTimestamp` back to WriteStorage level (`timestampTracker.Commit()`) so it tracks all incoming samples before queue selection\n2. **Track dropped samples separately** - Maintain `dataDropped` counter for dropped-by-relabel samples separately from `dataIn`\n3. **Adjust shard calculation formula** - Include `dataKeptRatio` to account for relabeling:\n   ```go\n   dataKeptRatio = dataOutRate / (dataDropped.rate() + dataOutRate)\n   desiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate * dataKeptRatio + backlogCatchup)\n   ```\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\nTo confirm this is the root cause:\n\n1. **Check timestamp metrics during resharding:**\n   ```\n   prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_timestamp_seconds  # Should not reset to 0\n   prometheus_remote_storage_queue_highest_sent_timestamp_seconds  # Should advance\n   ```\n\n2. **Monitor reshape transitions:**\n   - Watch for log line: \"Remote storage resharding from=X to=Y\"\n   - Check if `prometheus_remote_storage_shards_desired` increases during high load\n   - Verify samples flow continues during resharding\n\n3. **Load test scenarios:**\n   - Enable slow remote backend\n   - Set low queue capacity\n   - Force frequent target discovery changes\n   - Verify samples reach destination without stalling\n\n### Verification\n\nThe fix in commit 6806b68 successfully addresses this by:\n- Restoring per-WriteStorage `samplesIn` EWMA rate tracking\n- Adding per-WriteStorage `highestTimestamp` via `timestampTracker.Commit()`\n- Maintaining `dataDropped` separately for dropped samples\n- Running the `samplesIn.tick()` at WriteStorage level via goroutine\n- Passing both `samplesIn` and `highestTimestamp` to each QueueManager\n\nThis ensures resharding calculations use consistent, non-stale metrics across all queues.\n",

# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure

## Summary

The resharding stall occurs due to a race condition in the sharding metric calculations introduced in commit 184c7eb ("storage/remote: compute highestTimestamp and dataIn at QueueManager level"). When shards are computed at the QueueManager level rather than the WriteStorage level, the `highestTimestamp` metric becomes stale during resharding transitions, causing the `calculateDesiredShards()` function to incorrectly calculate shard requirements and potentially stall when queues are full.

## Root Cause

**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1152-1224` (calculateDesiredShards function)

The root cause is a data collection and timing mismatch introduced when resharding logic moved timestamp tracking from WriteStorage-level to QueueManager-level:

1. **Metric Location Change:** In commit 184c7eb, `highestTimestamp` moved from `metrics.highestTimestamp` (WriteStorage-wide) to `qm.highestRecvTimestamp` (per QueueManager). This per-queue metric is updated only when samples are **enqueued into the shard** (line 1380 in queue_manager.go).

2. **Race Condition During Resharding:** When resharding occurs (shards.stop() → shards.start()), the following happens:
   - Old shards are shut down, draining their queues
   - New shards are created and started
   - During this transition, **samples arriving at WriteStorage are temporarily routed to the old shard instances**
   - The new QueueManager's `highestRecvTimestamp` doesn't reflect samples from the old shards because they were already enqueued to the old instance
   - This creates a timestamp gap

3. **Incorrect Shard Calculation:** In `calculateDesiredShards()` at lines 1167-1171:
   ```go
   highestRecv     = t.highestRecvTimestamp.Get()  // Per
... (truncated)
